And Claim That an American Pastor Transmitted Messages for Ma Zhanshan

The Osaka Mainichi Shimbun says that New York Times reporter Steele and German Welt am Sonntag reporter Lindt, bearing the mission of the investigation team, secretly met with Ma Zhanshan and, entrusted by Ma Zhanshan, carried documents and intelligence, which were delivered by American pastor Leonard to Zhifu. In addition to instructing Manchukuo to lodge a protest with the American Consul General, they also accused him of concealing Steele and refusing extradition. Ma's subordinates have 16,000 cavalry, 14,000 infantry, and 36 artillery pieces, but their aircraft operation is not very skilled. Ma's strategy is to avoid large-scale warfare, only using small units for contact. Ma also said that if his subordinates run out of ammunition, they should also fight the enemy with guns and knives, vowing not to slacken."

The First Sound of Civil War in Guangdong Province 89

A Glimpse of the Fierce Battle Between Land and Sea Forces at Tangjiawan

Guangzhou Dispatch: Chen Ce's fleet, after the uproar over Chen Jitang's incorporation, part of it sailed far to Hainan, and part anchored at Tangjiawan in Zhongshan Port. There were about ten ships in Tangjiawan, all shallow-water river vessels. Therefore, since the opposition to the incorporation, these ten or so ships have been cruising around Tangjiawan in Zhongshan Port. Recently, Chen Jitang ordered the use of force to resolve the non-compliant fleet. In addition to transferring the Guard Brigade and the Three Independent Regiments to concentrate in Leizhou, preparing to cross the sea to attack Hainan, he also considered the shallow-water ships in Tangjiawan as a thorn in his side. Therefore, the first step was to find a way to eliminate the fleet there, and then use troops against Hainan. In advance, he secretly ordered Liang Gongfu's unit of the Second Regiment of the Training Division to arrive in Shiqi, Zhongshan on the 11th and 12th. From Shiqi, they took the Qiguan bus to Qian Shan, Xiangzhou, Beishan, Baishi, Songlin and other strategic locations to garrison. On the evening of the 13th, they advanced from Qian Shan to Wanzai, opposite Macau. At the same time, heavy troops were deployed in Qian Shan, Beishan, and other places, digging trenches, deploying artillery positions, and erecting many seven-and-a-half-inch retreat tube cannons, controlling the sea surface of Tangjiawan in a triangle, preparing to encircle Chen Ce's fleet from three sides when it arrived, hoping to capture all the ships there. He also consulted with the Macau government in advance, stating that if a battle occurred and the fleet tried to flee to the waters near Macau, it should not be sheltered or protected, otherwise, the Guangdong army would not bear any responsibility. Once the deployment was complete, on the evening of the 16th, the Feipeng, a small ship belonging to Chen Ce, sailed to the sea off Qian Shan. On the morning of the 17th, the Hushang, Pingxi, and Haikang ships arrived successively, anchoring in Tangwan. At this time, Liang's troops stationed in the three key locations in Tangwan used signal flags to order the four ships to disarm and return to the team. The four ships ignored the order. Liang Gongfu then ordered the troops in Qian Shan, Beishan, and Wanzai to launch a fierce attack on the four ships. The Pingxi and Hushang ships also returned fire in defense. They fought fiercely for an hour, and the sound of gunfire was like a continuous string of firecrackers. Later, the ships, without reinforcements, retreated while fighting, heading out to sea towards Macau. Liang opened fire with guns and cannons from Wanzai in Macau, and stray bullets flew everywhere. The Macau government sent Detective Chief Shi to cross the sea to negotiate with Liang's troops, requesting a cease-fire. Liang's troops stated that they had consulted with the Macau government in advance, prohibiting them from accommodating fleeing ships, and that if they did not stop them now, they would naturally not be responsible. Shi's negotiation was ineffective, so he returned and negotiated with Pan Guoliu, the commander of the four ships, requesting that he lead the four ships away from Macau to avoid implicating the people of Macau. Pan, with no base in Macau, ordered the ships to set sail from Macau, steaming towards Jilong Bay. As for the Marine Corps stationed in Zhongshan, to avoid conflict, they had already moved to Dasen Mountain in Baicao, Sanzao in the county. (Evening of June 18)

Chen Jitang Orders Troops in Fujian and Jiangxi to Return to Guangdong 90

The Third Army on the Fujian Border Has Returned to Xingning, Chaozhou, and Meizhou

Fan's Brigade in Southern Jiangxi Returns to Shaozhou; The First Army Continues to Return

Guangxi Troops Will Detour Through the Hunan-Guangdong Border to Suppress Bandits in Jiangxi

Guangzhou Dispatch: The First Army Group under Chen Jitang's command has been suppressing bandits on the border of Jiangxi and Fujian for several months. Its troop deployment includes the Third Army's Li Yangjing's ten regiments, the Independent First Division's Huang Renhuan's six regiments, and the Independent Second Division's Zhang Ruigui's six regiments on the eastern Jiangxi-Fujian border. In the northern Jiangxi area, the First Army's Yu Hanmou's seven regiments, the Second Army's Xiang Hanping's Fourth Division's Zhang Meixin's three regiments, the Independent First Brigade's Fan Dexing's three regiments, and the Independent Second Brigade's Chen Zhang's three regiments have entered Jiangxi. Recently, due to the tense situation, the various units on the Jiangxi-Fujian border have been successively withdrawn to take a defensive position. As the 19th Route Army gradually arrived in Fujian, Chen Jitang ordered the Third Army's various independent regiments, such as the First Independent Regiment's Zhao Lan's unit, the Second Independent Regiment's Xie Zheng's unit, the Third Independent Regiment's Deng Hui's unit, and the Fourth Independent Regiment's Luo Guichun's unit, to be successively transferred back to Dapu and Chaoan to garrison. Huang Renhuan's division will return from Wuping and Shanghang to Jiaoling and Pingyuan. The Third Army's Eighth Division's Huang Zhiwen's unit will concentrate in Meixian. The division's 24th Regiment's Chen Fengshao's unit, stationed in Shanghang, the 22nd Regiment's Ye Shouyao's unit, stationed in Pingyuan, and Xie Zheng's regiment, had already withdrawn to Xingning successively on the 12th of this month. The Seventh Division's Huang Yanzhen's unit also withdrew to the upper reaches of the Han River. As for the northern Jiangxi area, the units that had entered Jiangxi first withdrew the Independent First Brigade's Fan Dexing's unit, stationed in Niedu. It was found that Fan's brigade was directly commanded by Chen Jitang. After receiving the order, it immediately set off to return to Guangdong. The First Regiment's Chen Boying's unit arrived in Shaoguan on the 14th, the Second Regiment's Liao Daoming's unit returned to Renhua, and the Third Regiment's Qiu Guixin's unit returned to Shixing, expected to arrive on the 17th and 18th. Administrative Reform in Five Provinces Amidst Bandit Suppression 91

Specifying Standards for the Appointment of County Magistrates

Effectively Organizing Bandit Suppression Teams

Hankou Dispatch: The Lushan Conference decided on a policy of political and military progress in bandit suppression. It is believed that if military and political affairs cannot be coordinated, the follow-up matters after the recapture of bandit areas will be slow, and they will eventually fall back into the hands of bandits. Therefore, to completely eliminate the Red bandits, a thorough reform of politics is necessary. I recently met with Zhu Huaibing, the director of the Department of Civil Affairs. According to him, at this Lushan Conference, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, in view of the past bandit suppression in the five provinces of Central China, held separately, and the schemes and regulations implemented were also different. Now, it is necessary to plan uniformly to facilitate progress and to use political forces to assist military progress. For the recovery of bandit areas, special emphasis is placed on political construction. The current bandit suppression and village cleansing regulations in the five provinces are consulted with each other, taking their strengths and discarding their weaknesses. Among them, more laws are taken from Hunan Province. It is also heard that Zhu stated that the Lushan Conference decided on three major cases belonging to the administrative scope, which were shown to a certain party: (1) The standards for the appointment of county magistrates in bandit areas are determined to be those who are 30 years old or older and have the following qualifications: 1. Those who have served as recommended officials for more than two years and have rich military knowledge and experience; 2. Those who have made definite contributions to bandit suppression and communist eradication and have achieved results in handling administrative affairs, as certified by their direct superiors; (2) The methods for rewarding and punishing administrative personnel at all levels in bandit areas shall be handled in accordance with the regulations on rewarding and punishing administrative personnel at all levels during the bandit suppression period. However, in the following circumstances, they may be punished in accordance with military law: 1. Those who flee upon hearing the alarm or leave their posts without permission, resulting in the loss of cities; 2. Those who allow bandit forces to enter without taking measures to prevent them, resulting in devastation in the area; 3. Those who accept bribes to release bandits or negligently release well-known bandit leaders; (3) The organization of local self-defense teams in each county shall be completed within a time limit. The outline of the implementation methods for each county to form security corps or security brigades is as follows (including seven provinces such as Hubei, Henan, Anhui, Hunan, Jiangxi, Fujian, and Guangdong): 1. The existing security regiments and standing teams in each county shall be temporarily compiled into security corps or security brigades during the cleansing period after the Department of Civil Affairs or the Security Office investigates the situation and considers it appropriate; 2. The security corps or security brigades in each county shall be divided into two types, A and B. Their organizational structure is as stipulated below. A type security corps shall have jurisdiction over nine or more squadrons, and a B type security corps shall have jurisdiction over six or more squadrons up to less than nine squadrons. A type security brigade shall have jurisdiction over four or more squadrons up to less than six squadrons, and a B type security brigade shall have jurisdiction over two or more squadrons up to less than four squadrons. In addition, Commander-in-Chief Chiang also believed that the team handling in Hunan Province was very good. On the 22nd, he sent a telegram from Lushan to the governments and bandit suppression commanders in the provinces of Hubei, Jiangxi, Anhui, and Henan, ordering them to uniformly follow the Hunan Province method in areas where the bandit atmosphere is more intense, and to organize communist eradication volunteer forces within a time limit to increase the people's self-defense forces. (June 22)

Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces Jointly Issue Silk Industry Bonds 92

The Fixed Amount is 2.2 Million Yuan

Hangzhou Dispatch: Zhou Junyan, Director of the Department of Finance, and Zeng Yangfu, Director of the Department of Construction, believe that the silk industry in Zhejiang Province has been declining in recent years, resulting in abnormal withering of agriculture, industry, and commerce. This year, affected by the Shanghai War, the silk industry is in an even more precarious situation. They convened leaders from the silk, silk fabrics, banking, and other industries in the province to discuss relief measures, but their ability was limited and the effect was minimal. Now, with the consent of the Jiangsu Provincial Government and the approval of the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry, they plan to jointly issue a type of Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Industry Bond in the names of the two provinces, with a fixed amount of 2.2 million yuan and a monthly interest rate of 5%, with principal and interest to be repaid in 50 months. The funds for paying principal and interest will be allocated monthly by the Ministry of Finance from the funds under the reduction and exemption agreement between the National Goods Bank in Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces. The following are excerpts from the regulations of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Industry Bond:

(Article 1) This bond shall be issued by the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces and shall be named the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Industry Bond of the Republic of China in 1932. (Article 2) The amount of this bond shall be 2.2 million yuan. (Article 3) The purpose of this bond shall be solely for the relief of the silk and cocoon industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. (Article 4) The monthly interest rate of this bond shall be 5%. (Article 5) This bond shall be issued in June 1932. (Article 6) This bond shall be issued at 100% of its face value. (Article 7) The principal and interest of this bond shall be repaid in 50 months. Starting from June 1932, 44,000 yuan of principal shall be repaid monthly, with interest paid once, and the interest shall decrease as the principal decreases, until the principal and interest are fully repaid by the end of August 1936. (Article 8) The funds for paying the principal and interest of this bond shall be designated from the funds allocated by the Ministry of Finance for the reduction and exemption agreement between Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. The amount payable monthly according to the repayment schedule of this bond shall be allocated monthly by the National Goods Bank designated by the Ministry of Finance to the Fund Management Committee of this bond for payment until the principal and interest are paid off, and shall not be changed. (Article 9) The Fund Management Committee of this bond shall handle the payment of interest and principal, and shall designate the Central Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, the Local Bank of Jiangsu as the agencies for paying the principal and interest. (Article 10) This bond shall be of the bearer type. (Article 11) This bond shall be issued in two denominations: 1,000 yuan and 100 yuan. (Article 12) This bond may be freely mortgaged and traded. When it is necessary to pay security deposits for other official purposes, it may be used as collateral. (Article 13) If there is any forgery or damage to the credit of this bond, the judicial organs shall punish it according to law. (Article 14) These regulations shall be promulgated and implemented by the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces after being approved by the Ministry of Finance and put on record. (June 23)

The Financial Difficulties of Gansu Province 93

Teachers in Various Schools Go on Strike to Demand Back Pay

Lanzhou Dispatch: Gansu Province's financial income cannot make ends meet, and the difficulties have reached the extreme. Before Shao Lizi took office, the province's income for this year had been almost entirely used up, and the education expenses were in arrears for more than 20 months. Since Shao took office, he has tried his best to raise funds. Before the Dragon Boat Festival, each agency was paid one month's expenses, but the teachers and staff of the schools demanded back pay, requesting to be paid three months' arrears. However, the provincial treasury was empty, and the authorities had no ability to turn lead into gold, and did not agree to their request, which led to a strike. Shao stated that he has always attached great importance to education, but the arrears did not start with him. This time, one month's expenses were paid to all agencies, which had already exhausted his efforts, and how could he take care of the old debts? He earnestly persuaded the schools, and it is said that the teachers and staff of the schools have been able to understand the authorities' difficulties, and there is talk of resuming classes immediately.

Water Patrol Team Arrests Suspects: After the Songjiang Branch of the China Xingye Bank at Yue Miao Kou was robbed on the 21st, the society was shocked. Rape Attempt Leads to Assault and Charges: Zhang, the wife of Gong Yuelong, a villager in Yangrun Village, Xiaokunshan, Ninth District of the county, is somewhat attractive. Recently, Jin Xinglou, a fellow villager, became infatuated with her. Taking advantage of Gong Yuelong's absence on business, Jin sneaked into Zhang's house, intending to commit indecent acts. Refugee Shelter Closes: The refugee shelter in Songjiang during the national crisis closed last month. The current surplus of more than 1,500 yuan is used to elect a responsible custodian to store the pawnshop, which will be used as expenses for opening a vagrant craft training center in the future.

Gaoyou 102

Many Collapses on the Newly Built Canal Embankment: The canal embankment in Jiangbei was extensively built this spring. However, the newly built embankment often collapses. Now that the canal embankment project is about to be completed, unexpectedly, in the past two days, many collapses have occurred along the canal. It is estimated that more than ten zhang of the military tower and more than ten zhang of the South Gate have collapsed. More than 40 zhang of the Xin embankment have collapsed. If there is flooding in the autumn, the embankment is very worrying.

Chairman of the Chamber of Commerce Accused of Thorough Investigation: Liu Zhiren, the chairman of the County Chamber of Commerce, has now been accused by Chen Shu and other members of the association to the Provincial Party Headquarters for concealing the by-election. The department has now ordered the County Party Headquarters to thoroughly investigate and report the truth for verification.

Xiaoshan 103

People Oppose Autonomous Household Donation: Since County Magistrate Du implemented the Xiaoshan Autonomous Household Donation, the disadvantages have appeared without any benefits. The district township chiefs have used this as an excuse to strictly collect it. The district township offices are no different from a collection agency, collecting from east to west, causing unbearable harassment. But there are no achievements in autonomous work. Now, the people of the county are complaining and hate it.

Adulterer and Adulteress Each Sentenced to Death: The County Court began a public trial on the 22nd for the case of Cao Cai's murder of Shi Village in Caocai Meisheng outside the South Gate of Xiaoshan. Cao and her lover Cao Achuan were defended by the assigned lawyers Ma Junpu and Nai Xiang. As a result, the adulterer and adulteress and the accomplice Cao Chuanlai were all sentenced to death. There are still accomplices such as Cao Arong wanted for strict punishment.

[Letter L

Public Letter from the First District Office of Songjiang County 104

Respectfully, I have read the article "Alley Lawsuit" in the Songjiang Dispatch in your newspaper on the 21st, which is slightly inconsistent with the facts. Initially, Zhang Lianquan, the chief of Nanwai Town, according to a letter from Gu Yingfu, said that Yao Runmin invaded the construction circle and the underground drainage ditch, which was considered to hinder public interest and traffic. He transferred to our office to investigate and stop him from coming. When the prevention of obstructing public interest and blocking traffic concerns the public interest, our district chief serves the village and intends to use personal emotions to find ways to dredge the solution, so that both sides can be balanced. He went to the town with the town chief to investigate and survey, but he did not meet Gu Yingfu because he was out. Later, according to Yao Runmin, the case of building an underground drainage ditch was concluded after three trials by the judiciary, and there was absolutely no obstacle to public interest and traffic. The construction circle is even more non-existent, etc. After investigation by our district chief, it was found that there was no error, and the construction of the drainage ditch had already undergone legal trial, and the procedures were complete, and there was nothing to criticize. The interview draft is very different from the facts. We are sincerely afraid of turning errors and transmitting errors, so we wrote a letter to explain in detail, hoping that you will give the column to publish the letter to show the truth. To the highest degree of public friendship, District Chief Zhong Taishi, June 22.

Special Document

To Those Advocating for Resuming Diplomatic Relations with Russia - Chen Qitian 105

And Questioning Shen Bao Reporter Mr. Chen Binhe (Part 3, Continued)

This line of argument seems to have transformed from the "resume relations" theory into a "communist" theory. I want to ask Mr. Chen for a clear answer: Are you merely advocating for resuming relations, or are you also advocating for communism? If you advocate for both resuming relations and communism, then I will debate the issue of communism with you. However, if you only advocate for resuming relations and oppose communism, then you should not use such ambiguous language and merely present one-sided arguments to confuse the ignorant. It is said that Shen Bao has a circulation of 130,000 copies, with at least 200,000 readers. It seems that a reporter for such a major newspaper should be particularly careful about the arguments and wording used in current affairs commentaries, and should be responsible for every statement made. Mr. Chen, you are a rising star reporter. I hope you cherish your future, do more to benefit the nation, and avoid future regrets. This is my sincere and well-intentioned advice, and I hope Mr. Chen will accept it. How many people supported the Communist Party six years ago? But what was the result? Take Mr. Chen Duxiu, for example. Was he not the most ardent promoter of communism and the longest-serving leader of the Communist Party? However, Russia said he did not support the policy of violent revolution, labeled him an "opportunist" and "liquidationist," and expelled him. Now, the Communists do not recognize him as a Communist Party member, and he is left hiding in the concessions with a few disgruntled comrades, occasionally uttering mournful cries. Russia used him up and then wanted to overthrow him to prevent him from becoming too powerful to control. I truly feel sorry for him, as he was merely a sacrifice for Russia. I also regret that he misled so many enthusiastic young people. My friend Mr. Yun Daiying had a 14-year friendship with me (from the first year to the fourteenth year of the Republic). I know he was capable and competent, truly a top-notch figure in the Communist Party. Last year, he came to Shanghai from Hubei to mediate internal conflicts within the Communist Party, but he was betrayed and killed by his comrades. Before his death, he told someone, "It is better that I die. The so-called communism of today is tens of thousands of miles away from my original ideals. The darkness and infighting within the Party are truly unbearable to witness and make it difficult for me to do the right thing. It is better to die sooner rather than later." When I heard this news, I deeply regretted his fate. What a talented person, merely sacrificed for Russia.

What I said seems to have strayed from the topic. Now, let's return to discussing with Mr. Chen whether we should immediately resume diplomatic relations with Russia, assuming that "the current state of China is the most suitable soil for communism." Before discussing this issue, we must recognize that there are two major categories of reasons for the rampant activities of Chinese communists: one is internal, arising from within, which is what Mr. Chen calls "soil"; the other is external, coming from Russia, which is Russia using the convenience of resumed diplomatic relations to instigate the activities of the Communist Party. If we want to save China and eliminate the communists, we must address both internal and external factors simultaneously, treating both the root and the symptoms. If we only guard against external factors without addressing internal ones, it would be like placing rotten objects in an iron box, which will eventually breed insects and even decay. If we only address internal factors without guarding against external ones, it would be like placing soil in the open air, allowing people to freely sow poisonous weeds and irrigate and fertilize them, enabling them to rapidly flourish and grow, to the point where touching them would cause widespread harm, making it impossible to save the situation. Therefore, we can revise Mr. Chen's article as follows to express our meaning:

The focus of the question is not only whether our country has soil suitable for communism and whether there are opportunities for communism to spread, but also whether Russia will use this soil and these opportunities to promote communism and aid the communists after resuming diplomatic relations. If, after resuming diplomatic relations, Russia can further use this soil and these opportunities to achieve the goal of communizing China, then immediately resuming diplomatic relations with Russia would only hasten China's demise. What benefit would there be? Ignoring the external factors of the problem and not asking about them at all is like opening the door to welcome thieves and recognizing robbers as one's own children, merely serving as propaganda for the bandits. Alas! Even if things are already rotten, placing them in an iron box may still breed insects. How can we not cherish them and allow poisonous bacteria to invade everywhere, hastening their death?

Now that "our country has no strong unified government," no "strict social organization," no "stable people's livelihood," and no "grasp on controlling communists," wanting to follow in the footsteps of the great powers, opening the door wide, and allowing "conspirators of red terror" to enter and exit freely is tantamount to allowing people to sow communist poisonous seeds on Chinese soil and then supporting and aiding their growth, making the red disaster impossible to contain. If our country wants to be saved, it must, on the one hand, eliminate national traitors and reform politics at its root, and on the other hand, resist foreign powers (including resisting Japan and severing relations with Russia) and eliminate the communists (the communists are Russia's plainclothes troops) to treat its symptoms. If we do not address both the root and the symptoms, and consider both internal and external factors, and want to use immediately resuming diplomatic relations with Russia as a temporary measure, is your vision not too short-sighted? (Note 3) (Note 4)

Note 1: Mr. Chen Binhe's five current affairs commentaries appeared in Shen Bao: (1) May 12, "Resuming Diplomatic Relations with the Soviet Union and Preventing Communism," (2) May 13, "From the International Situation to Sino-Russian Diplomatic Relations," (3) May 14, "A Third Discussion on Sino-Soviet Diplomatic Relations," (4) May 30, "Clarifying Doubts about Resuming Diplomatic Relations with the Soviet Union," (5) June 4, "Re-Clarifying Resuming Diplomatic Relations with the Soviet Union."

Note 2: The original text of Mr. Chen quoted in this article all comes from the above five articles. To save space, it is not specifically noted under each quotation. To clarify the arguments, the quoted sentences all follow the original text without any additions or deletions.

Note 3: The last paragraph is written in classical Chinese, which is inconsistent with the style of this article. Moreover, the use of pronouns to follow Mr. Chen's style is also not entirely satisfactory. However, in order to compare the differences and similarities in viewpoints and to determine right and wrong, it is attempted.

Note 4: The original plan for this article was to have another section to discuss in detail whether the reasons for resuming diplomatic relations mentioned in the previous five current affairs commentaries were sufficient, but after working on it for an entire night (from 7 pm on the 8th to 7 am on the 9th), I could not continue. I will tentatively use this article to have a preliminary discussion with Mr. Chen. When referring to Mr. Chen in the article, it always refers to Mr. Binhe and is not self-referential. (End)

Educational News - Important News

Central University's Movement for Financial Independence 106

Teacher and Student Representatives to Petition the National Government Next Tuesday

The funding for Central University has been suspended by the Jiangsu Education Funding Custody Office, and no solution has been found to date, causing great panic among the faculty and students. Therefore, five representatives were elected to handle the issue of financial independence. Yesterday, the first joint meeting was held in the left wing of the main hall of the university. The faculty representatives were He Haoruo, Zhang Qiyun, Zha Qian, Ding Sixian, and Miao Fenglin. The student representatives were Chen Cong, Yu Jizhong, Wang Shunxu, Jiang Xueqian, and Cao Chengwen. The results of the discussion are as follows: (1) The association is named the Joint Conference of Faculty and Student Representatives for the National Central University's Movement for Financial Independence. (2) Next week is designated as the university's Movement for Financial Independence Week. (3) Next Monday, during the memorial week, faculty and student representatives will report to the general assembly on the progress of the matter. (4) Next Monday at 4 pm, a reception will be held in the university's main hall for journalists from both within and outside Nanjing. (5) A declaration will be issued immediately to state the significance of this movement. (6) Next Tuesday morning, all faculty and student representatives will go to the National Government to petition. (7) The acting president will be notified by telegram of the progress of the fundraising efforts, and he will be asked to come south as soon as possible to lead the proceedings.

Suzhou Middle School Teachers' Association Holds Meeting to Demand Owed Salaries 107

Before the First Half of March's Salary is Fully Paid

Representatives to Occupy the Education Funding Management Office

The Suzhou Provincial Middle School Teachers' Association held a meeting yesterday at Zhenjiang Provincial Zhenjiang Middle School. More than 20 representatives from schools such as Songjiang Middle School attended. The meeting was chaired by Yan Xiaofan. The resolutions included: (1) The management office is required to issue one month's worth of funds before the colleagues disperse, and the remainder must be issued before July 15th. (2) Before the funds for the first half of March are fully paid, representatives from each school will occupy the management office. If this is not effective, the number of representatives must be increased. (3) Outstanding debts will be demanded from the Finance Department for repayment, and at least two-thirds of the arrears must be issued before July 15th. (4) The funding for schools affected by the war will be handled in the same way as other schools. Negotiations will be held with the Education Department. (5) It was decided that the representatives would gather at Nanjing Middle School on the 23rd. It is reported that after the meeting, the representatives petitioned both the Finance and Education Departments separately, but no concrete measures have yet been taken.

Qingdao University Adjourns Classes Early 108

Students Strike...Do Not Show Up For Exams

Qingdao, 22nd Telegram - The Qingdao University Student Self-Government Association submitted four demands to the university administration on the 16th: (1) Abolish dormitory fees, following the precedent of other universities; (2) Revise Article 43 of the academic regulations, which stipulates that students who fail three courses in a year, or two required courses, will be dismissed; (3) Remove unqualified teachers; (4) Open up the library for academic use. Because no definite response was received, a student strike was unanimously launched on the 22nd, and a declaration was issued stating the reasons. The university administration held an administrative meeting on the afternoon of the 22nd and decided that exams would be held as usual on the 23rd. Further measures would be decided if students did not take the exams.

Qingdao, 23rd Telegram - Qingdao University held exams at 9 am on the 23rd, but the students did not appear. The university administration issued a notice announcing that classes would be adjourned early from the 23rd to September 12th, when school would resume and make-up exams would be held. Remedial classes were scheduled to be held as usual on the 24th.

The Tragic Situation of Educational Destruction in Harbin by the Japanese Army 109

丨All Cultural Institutions Occupied and Objects Transported Away丨

丨News of Investigation Team Arriving in Harbin, Forcing Schools to Reopen丨

丨Switching to Japanese Textbooks Confuses Teachers and Students丨

According to a secret investigation report from a foreign agency to the diplomatic authorities, the situation of the destruction of education in Harbin by the Japanese army after their arrival is very detailed. The report is recorded as follows: After the Japanese army occupied the Northeast, they completely occupied elementary schools, middle schools, universities, and all levels of schools in various places, and destroyed the schools. For example, the buildings of the Second and Third Middle Schools in Harbin were very grand, and the internal equipment was also very complete. When the Japanese army arrived in Harbin, they completely occupied the elementary and middle schools, and all students and staff were expelled. The school buildings were damaged, and all valuable items inside were transported away. The courtyards were filled with soldiers, and sandbags were piled up in front of the gates. The cultural area was turned into a military camp, with armed guards as if facing a formidable enemy, which was very painful to witness. All cultural institutions and libraries in Harbin were occupied, and none were preserved. When the League of Nations investigation team arrived in Liaoning, there was news that they would go to Harbin. To avoid the team's attention, the Japanese temporarily moved the Japanese army out of the schools a few days in advance, and the sandbags in front of the gates were also removed. Teachers and students were notified and forced to reopen the schools. Teachers were urged and forced to go to school by name. Those who were unwilling to go or resigned were arrested and imprisoned. As for the textbooks used, whether in elementary or middle schools, they were not allowed to use the textbooks approved by the Ministry of Education of the National Government. Instead, all Japanese textbooks were used. Teachers and students were forced to go to school and listen to orders perfunctorily. In several elementary schools when classes started, the textbooks issued were all single articles. Students did not understand the meaning of the textbooks. When they asked the teachers, the teachers replied, "I don't understand either, just listen confusedly." The pain of enduring humiliation and seeking survival can be imagined. After class, most of the students ran away. In addition, the Japanese army would come to the schools to inspect from time to time and cause trouble for no reason. If they were dissatisfied, they would take the opportunity to make trouble and arrest people at any time. The 90th Elementary School in Xinzhengyang River was inspected by the Japanese army several times, and teachers were arrested for no reason. Principal Wang was even scolded by the Japanese army to his face, saying that he should pay attention in the future, otherwise, they would handle things in the same way, acting arrogantly and treating Chinese people as worse than subjugated slaves. Principal Li of Harbin Provincial Middle School said that one day the Japanese army went to the school and searched it extensively. When asked why they were searching, the Japanese soldiers said that because stones had fallen in front of them at the back gate of the school late at night while they were on patrol, they were searching and investigating strictly. The principal did not dare to speak. The next day, more than 30 Japanese soldiers came again to search. After the search, they told the principal that if there were any more acts of insulting the Japanese army, they would be shot (referring to the students and the principal). If Sanmin Zhuyi and Party doctrine books were found in the homes of students' families and people in the education sector, the Japanese army would burn the books after searching them and arrest and interrogate the people. The various kinds of unbearable situations are too numerous to mention. The tragic situation of national subjugation is even worse than in Korea and Annam, it is said.

Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau Announces the Examination Schedule for Qualification Verification 110

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau, in accordance with the instructions of the Ministry of Education, will hold qualification verification examinations for graduates and students of unapproved and closed private colleges and universities starting on July 1st. The deadline for registration was June 20th. A total of 73 people applied, of which 55 were approved to take the examination, 12 were required to submit supplementary documentation, 3 were required to take the pre-test for higher education, and 2 were not qualified to take the examination. Those who were required to submit supplementary documentation or whose procedures were incomplete have already been notified separately by letter. It is reported that the examination subjects and schedule have also been compiled and sent directly to each examinee. If they have not been received, they can be retrieved. The examination dates are July 1st, 2nd, and 3rd, from 8 am to 5 pm each day. The location is the Municipal Wuben Girls' Middle School on Huangjia Que Road, Ximen.

The County Education Bureau Held the Second Regular Meeting of the Administrative Committee Yesterday 111

Thirteen Important Proposals Resolved

The Administrative Committee of the Shanghai County Education Bureau held its second regular meeting yesterday afternoon. The attendees were Qin Yanqi, Chen Pingyi, Peng Liren, Jia Fore, Zhu Hange, Yao Huiquan, Xue Huikang, Yan Shenyu, Zhang Yi, Shi She, Ding Renke, and Zhu Chunsheng. The meeting was chaired by Qin Yanqi, and the minutes were recorded by Pan Shengshan. The proceedings were conducted as prescribed. The report items were omitted. Discussion items: (1) A proposal to review and approve the bureau's budget and policy plan for the 21st year of the Republic. It was resolved that Chen Pingyi, Zhu Chunsheng, and Yao Huiquan would be appointed as members to conduct the review. (2) A proposal on how to formulate the standards for increasing, decreasing, paying, and deducting primary school funds in accordance with the provincial decree. It was resolved that, as there are still many obstacles to this proposal, the Education Bureau should submit a written reply based on the following reasons and implement them in practice. Reason 1: The salaries of teachers and staff in schools in this area are already very meager. Reason 2: The level of students in the urban area of this county is generally higher than in other counties. Reason 3: Losses from recent wars cannot be further reduced. (3) Omitted. (4) A proposal to continue sponsoring children from this county to study in vocational schools and vocational departments and requesting instructions from the schools. It was resolved that the original method would be amended and passed, and the following schools would be designated: 1. Agricultural Department: Provincial Suzhou Agricultural School; 2. Engineering Department: Zhonghua Vocational School; 3. Business Department: Provincial Shanghai Middle School. (5) A proposal to provide relief to rural teachers, "Proposed by the Education Association": (A) Scholarships for the children of poor teachers; (B) Building a public cemetery for teachers; (C) Providing life insurance for all teachers in the county; (D) Establishing savings plans for teachers; (E) Stipulating regulations for teachers' rest and recuperation. It was resolved that the principles would be approved, and the Education Bureau would coordinate with the Education Association to gradually implement them based on the urgency of each issue. (6) A proposal to promote the relocation of Shanghai Middle School to the county area, "Proposed by the Education Association": (A) Forming a joint delegation of public organizations to contact Principal Zheng of Shanghai Middle School to discuss relocation methods; (B) Submitting opinions and requesting the provincial government to promptly order the principal of Shanghai Middle School to prepare for relocation; (C) Forming a joint organization of agencies and groups to establish a Shanghai Middle School Relocation Promotion Association responsible for promoting the relocation. It was resolved that the original method would be followed, and the County Education Association would actively proceed in conjunction with various public organizations. (7) A proposal to convert the county's rural normal school to a six-year system in accordance with the new system and to establish a affiliated kindergarten normal school, "Proposed by the Education Association": (A) Starting in the 21st year of the Republic, the county's rural normal school will be expanded to a six-year rural normal school in accordance with the new system; (B) A kindergarten normal school department will be established at the rural normal school to accept primary school graduates who are interested in education; (C) The funds for the rural normal school can be allocated separately from the funds for the kindergarten normal school under the heading of compulsory education funds. It was resolved that it would be retained. (8) A proposal to pilot rural simple primary schools or short-term primary schools, "Proposed by the Education Association": (A) School site: select a rural area with a concentrated population; (B) School building: borrow civilian houses or temples; (C) School land: cultivate one side of the land; (D) Equipment: use the principle of simplicity; (E) Teachers: hire those who love rural life and can endure hardship or have special skills; (F) Subjects: Chinese, arithmetic, general knowledge, work; (G) Life: emphasis on imparting knowledge in the morning and cultivating vocational skills in the afternoon; (H) Students: enroll out-of-school children and adults in rural areas aged ten to sixteen; (I) Funds: approximately 100 yuan for start-up costs and 360 yuan for recurring costs, to be provided by the County Education Bureau or raised locally; (J) Length of schooling: one or two years. It was resolved that it would be retained. (9) A proposal to promote locally produced cloth to relieve people's livelihood and cultivate a frugal lifestyle, "Proposed by the County Education Association". It was resolved that the County Education Bureau would instruct all educational institutions to follow it in light of local conditions. (10) A proposal that all levels of schools should pay attention to brush calligraphy. It was resolved that the Education Bureau would implement it by issuing an order. (11) A proposal that all levels of schools should pay attention to agricultural education, "Proposed by the County Education Association". (12) A proposal to emphasize women's craft education, "Proposed by the County Education Association". The above two proposals were discussed together. It was resolved that the principles would be approved, and the Education Bureau would handle them in light of the circumstances. (13) A request to designate the premises of the County Education Association, "Proposed by the Education Association": (A) Designate two rooms in the new county government office as the County Education Association's office; (B) Repair the old buildings near the new county government office to serve as the County Education Association's office; (C) Build a new house on the vacant land of Yongxing Nunnery in Zhuanqiao. It was resolved that the Director of the County Education Bureau would submit it to the County Government Conference for discussion.

Notes on Striking the Ancient Temple Bell (30) (2) - Not Removing the Weeds in the Courtyard, the Teacher's Wife 114

Thirty-Five

The three of us – Mr. Zhu, my younger brother, and I – went for a walk in the countryside. We saw Mrs. Chen washing clothes by the pond. Mr. Zhu pointed to the grass behind her and asked, "What does that mean?" I followed Mr. Zhu's direction and saw a lively little child sitting in a large basket! It turned out that this was Mrs. Chen's little treasure. There was no one at home to help take care of him, and she was afraid he would play in the water by the pond, so his mother had put him in a basket and asked him to sit there. Mrs. Chen would wash a few times and then turn around to look at him. Mr. Zhu asked, "Are there many cases like this?" I said, "One morning, Aunt Sun came to the temple with a small stool in her left hand and her four-year-old daughter in her right hand. She said, 'Bell! I need to pick firewood and sell it in the city. I'm entrusting Qiaogu to your care for half a day. Just have her sit on the stool and don't let her run around.' This kind of thing is common. Most people entrust their children to neighbors and relatives to take care of them." Mr. Zhu played with the little baby in the basket for a while, then walked and thought. Suddenly, he said excitedly, "Bell! We've discovered a new continent today! I see that the little baby in the basket is a burden for Mrs. Chen. Qiaogu is the same burden for Aunt Sun. And there are many more like those who follow their mothers and grandmothers around like tails, making them anxious." I said, "You are right, sir. These children are only three to five years old, they can't herd cattle, they can't cut grass, they can't deliver meals. They are in the way at home, and when they go out, they are a burden. Rural women are indeed overwhelmed. Why are you so happy about this? What new continent have you discovered?"

Mr. Zhu said, "These children don't have all those difficulties you mentioned. Crying, hugging, whining, peeing, pooping – their bodily functions are not a big problem. If we have a place for these children to play, their mothers can entrust them there and go to work with peace of mind. And if they bring them in the morning and pick them up in the evening, they will feel as if they haven't seen each other for a long time, and the love and happiness between mother and child can be imagined. In the city, places that take care of children like this are called nurseries and kindergartens. Nurseries and kindergartens in the countryside are truly in their element! The countryside is the new continent of nurseries and kindergartens!"

World Games 116

丨Ministry of Education Sends Personnel to Attend丨

丨Consul General in San Francisco to Represent丨

Italy Resolves to Adopt Elite Doctrine

United Kingdom and Canada Proceeding Secretly

Finland Confident in Long-Distance Running and Throwing

Nanjing, 23rd Telegram - The 10th World Games are scheduled to be held from July 30th to August 14th in Los Angeles, California, USA. The Ministry of Education has requested our embassy in the United States to appoint the Consul General in San Francisco to attend on its behalf. The International Technical Education Conference is scheduled to be held in Brussels from September 26th to 28th. The Ministry of Education has requested the Minister to Belgium to send personnel to participate on its behalf.

Italy: The country's preparations for this Olympics have adopted the elite doctrine. The events in which it has been decided to compete are: (1) Athletics (only track events), 6 swimmers, 8 boxers, 8 cyclists, and fencing (undetermined). The above five sports are what the country is traditionally confident in. At the previous Amsterdam Games, boxing, which had 5 victories in 8 events, and fencing, which had 2 victories, should select promising athletes to participate in the Games this time.

United Kingdom: The country's dark horses may be more numerous than those of other countries. The preparations for the events appear calm on the surface, but in reality, they are not to be underestimated. It is said that it has been decided to select 120 skilled athletes for various events.

Finland: The country is most confident in long-distance running and throwing. The leader of long-distance running is expected to secure past glory. In addition to the above two sports, Finland's decathlon and pentathlon athletes have also broken world records, and outstanding newcomers are emerging, so they will not fall behind in this competition.

Canada: At the 1928 Amsterdam Games, Canada's track short-distance running was admired by the world. For this Games, they had already sent inspectors to Los Angeles to conduct on-site investigations and actively prepare. However, the country has always maintained a silent attitude, and the final selections have not been completed. It is vaguely heard that the events they are participating in are the triple jump, long jump, and short-distance running. Other events are still being pre-selected and have not yet been announced.

Wimbledon Tennis Championships, Day Three 118

Mrs. Marti's Undiminished Prowess…Tennis King Cochet Suffers Crushing Defeat

London, 22nd – The third day of the Wimbledon World Tennis Championships saw the start of the men's doubles. Free Talk

King of Han Wei Nu 125

Those who wear clogs avoid mentioning the word "Wo," especially "Wo Nu." If we call them "Wo Nu," they will retort and write "Shina Wo Nu" on the walls.

According to Shuowen Jiezi, the character "Wo" (倭) is a phono-semantic compound, with "ren" (人, person) as the semantic component and "wei" (委) as the phonetic component. The characters "Wo" and "Wei" originally had no different pronunciations and were used interchangeably in ancient times. The seal above, with the five characters "King of Han Wei Nu" (漢委奴國王) in white seal script, is copied from the Japanese book "Kinsekishi." According to the Japanese book "Kogorajiroku," "The seal is made of gold, with a snake as the handle. It is slightly less than eight fen square and five li thick, weighing twenty-nine qian. It was excavated in the fourth year of Tenmei (1784), under a giant rock in the ground of Shiga Island, Naka County, Chikuzen Province." The fourth year of Tenmei corresponds to the nineteenth year of the Qianlong reign of the Qing Dynasty. As for the year the seal was granted, it is recorded in the Book of the Later Han: "In the second year of the Zhongyuan reign of Emperor Guangwu, the Wo Nu Kingdom offered tribute and paid homage, and Emperor Guangwu bestowed upon them a seal and ribbon." It is likely this very gold seal. When the Han people were strong, bestowing upon them the seal of the King of Wei Nu was an immense honor for them. Even now, they still treat it as a treasure, recorded in the accounts of archaeologists, as precious as the celestial sphere, the Yellow River Map, the red sword, and the great instruction!

Alas! The great Han people, now, when we call them "Wo Nu," they retort! They even offer us the four characters "Shina Wo Nu"! If our countrymen do not strive for self-improvement, we will truly become Shina Wo Nu! Compatriots with blood in your veins! Is it painful? Is it not painful? Is it shameful? Is it not shameful?

The Calligraphy of Party and State Leaders 126

— Zizai

Chinese calligraphy is different from that of other countries. Seal script, clerical script, regular script, and cursive script each have their own wonders, vigorous, refined, and elegant. Characters are transmitted through people. In addition to accomplishments, character is especially important. This article only discusses the calligraphy of party and state leaders, and not others, as an aid to conversations over tea and wine. In the past, Tan Zuan'an's family collected many of Nanyuan Songchan's works. He would copy them in his spare time, wielding the brush with ease. He liked to write for others, but those without a connection were often done by Yue Sen. Yu Youren liked to wield the brush before bed in the evening, free and unrestrained, creating his own style. His nephew Zhou Bomin's imitation was very similar, almost indistinguishable (eight or nine out of ten of the Yu Youren calligraphy printed by the China Commercial Press were written by Zhou). Zhang Jingjiang (was especially good at landscape painting), Wang Jingwei, and Ye Yuhu were all skilled in calligraphy, but they were quite conceited and did not easily write for others. Hu Hanmin's copying of the Cao Quan Stele was very profound, rigorous, and simple, the characters like the man. In recent years, Dai Jitao devoted himself to practicing calligraphy, liking to write on bird-silk grids, quite neat and elegant. Wu Zhihui's seal script and Xu Shiying's running script each reached their own perfection. Zhang Xueliang used to practice seal script diligently in the Northeast, still without vulgarity. As for Li Liejun, he lacked dominance, and Chu Minyi tended towards vulgarity (only responding to every request, the opposite of his brother-in-law Jingwei). Shao Yuancong was too artificial, Wang Boqun's fiery temperament had not dissipated. Cai Yuanpei, Yang Shukan, Ma Junwu, Zou Lu, and Yi Peiji each formed their own style, recognizable at a glance. Niu Yongjian was originally a military man, his characters without dominance, but he did not write easily. Xu Qian was extremely confident in his calligraphy, having written nineteen methods of using the brush, saying what others had not said. Those who study calligraphy may wish to read it. Lin Zichao, Tang Shaochuan, Sun Zhesheng, Kong Xiangxi, and others all had their trusted aides write on their behalf, such as Yi Dachang on behalf of Tang and Liang Hancao on behalf of Sun. Li Jishen, Chen Mingshu, Feng Yuxiang, Zhang Zhijiang, Hu Zongduo, Ma Fuxiang, Liu Wendao, etc., also wrote from time to time. Due to their rank and learning, their military character was revealed in their ink. Others such as Jing Ziyuan's 　Baozi, Liu San's Shimen Ode, Lin Zhixian's Han stele, Xie Wuliang and Liu Yazi's running script, Ru Yuli and Zhou Bonian's Wei stele, Wang Luyi and Ma Yichu's small regular script, each had their own strengths and were all worth seeing. They can be transmitted not because they are in the party and state.

World Short News 127

— Haike

Regarding the Peace Army: A British weekly said that recently, in view of the intensity of the Sino-Japanese war in the Far East, which is not a blessing for world peace, someone proposed organizing a large peace army to interpose between the two armies to stop the fighting. This was originally a good idea, and there was a precedent in history. After the Roman Empire embraced Christianity, the bloody gladiatorial contests were still a popular pastime for most people. One day, during a gladiatorial contest, a Christian monk named Telemachus jumped into the arena and threw himself between the two gladiators to stop the bloodshed. Unfortunately, the monk's good intentions were in vain, and he was killed by the two men. However, this tragic impression was deeply imprinted in the minds of the people, and the gladiatorial contests were later abolished. However, this kind of story cannot be applied to modern times. Therefore, whether the Peace Army will be effective is still a question. The most reliable messengers of peace should still be the international bankers, who refuse all loans for military equipment.

Ueda Ashamed to See Off Friends and Relatives 128

— Gongyu

During the January 28th Incident, Saltzawa, the Japanese naval commander stationed in Shanghai, was emboldened by the Mukden Incident, believing that the Chinese army would not dare to resist, and even if they did, they would not last long and could be resolved in four hours. Therefore, he rashly launched an attack. Unexpectedly, the resistance of the 19th Route Army was so fierce that the Japanese naval landing force, combined with 6,000 local Japanese, was routed. If it were not for the concessions as a shield, the entire army would have been annihilated. The Japanese government then ordered Nomura to lead reinforcements to Shanghai. At that time, the Japanese were still extraordinarily confident, as if Nomura's arrival would immediately resolve the 19th Route Army. When other countries offered to mediate, they said that Lieutenant General Nomura was a peaceful politician and would not allow the situation to escalate. Nomura also said to foreign reporters, "In another seven days, our work in Shanghai will be finished." Such was his arrogance. However, after several attacks, they were still defeated. The Japanese government was shocked and realized that our army could not be taken lightly. They urgently ordered the elite 9th Division to go to aid, appointing Division Commander Ueda Kenkichi as commander. Ueda was quite confident. When he left, his spirits were particularly high, making all kinds of boasts to those who saw him off, firmly believing that as soon as he arrived in Shanghai, he could drive our army out of the Shanghai area. Who would have thought that after a half-month of fierce fighting, he would still be defeated and unable to gain an inch? It was not until he was replaced by Shirakawa Yoshinori, with an even larger number of troops, that they saw our thin defenses at Liuhe. They secretly dispatched a large army to land and attack our army's rear, forcing our army to retreat completely to the second line of defense overnight, without leaving a single soldier or a single weapon. Westerners praised this as a miracle. However, when it came to rewarding merit, it was attributed to Shirakawa. Therefore, when Shirakawa was dying, the Japanese Emperor bestowed upon him the title of Baron, while Ueda was not included. Now Ueda has returned to Japan. A friend wrote to me, saying that he is quite ashamed to see the friends and relatives who saw him off in the past. When someone mentions the Shanghai battle, he shakes his head and says nothing. So, from now on, will the Japanese dare to be arrogant again and treat us as if we are nothing?

Discussion on Researching Chinese Medicine 129

— Shen Jiliang

When I was studying medicine in Chiba, Japan, I heard a lecture by a German pharmacologist who mentioned our country in one section, roughly saying that due to geographical reasons, China's medicinal products are mostly plants. Although they have not undergone scientific procedures, their efficacy is often not weaker than the mineral drugs in Europe and America that are purely chemically synthesized. From this, we can see the value of natural resources. If we add artificial research, what will the results be? Unfortunately, in China's five thousand years, there has only been Shennong. If I were given ten years, I would travel all over China, and I know that the secrets I would uncover would be quite impressive, and so on. His words were exaggerated and full of criticism, deeply causing me and my peers shame and resentment. But the fact is so. At that time, it was truly difficult to find one person in our country who was capable of inventing new drugs. Until recently, the people of our country have gradually been able to demonstrate their abilities. In Shanghai alone, there are already many new drugs that have been created and introduced to the world. However, those who fail are often numerous. Are these people all deceiving the world with fake drugs? According to my research, there are quite a few that are far superior to imported products, but ultimately difficult to succeed. This is because the founders are ignorant of righteousness and profit, fond of greatness and success, and in the way of research, do not know what is called striving for perfection. Their failure is appropriate. The owner of Shanghai Peisheng Pharmaceutical Company is committed to the Lung-Benefiting and Gold-Nourishing Herb. We have long known that it was invented several generations ago and collected from thousands of miles away. He spares no major sacrifices to seek a radical cure for those with lung diseases. This is deeply in line with the indomitable spirit of European and American creators. Therefore, I was always concerned about the words of a certain pharmacologist in the past. Now I am relieved and have no regrets.

Short News: The Zhongcheng Art Society at No. 672 Old Rougemont Road recently invented a kind of silhouette painting. It is matched with an artistic frame and is very unique. Placed in the room, it adds a lot of color. It is also quite suitable as a gift. It is said that the Meimei Company at the intersection of Jing'an Temple Road and Mohawk Road and the Chunji Tang in the Penglai Market all sell it.

Battalion Commander Li's Wearing of Flowers 130

— Yanmeng

A week ago, I, through the introduction of a friend, went specifically to Longhua Hospital to visit a wounded battalion commander who is still in bed. A fair face, a short and stocky figure, handsome eyebrows, such a brave shadow flashed into my eyes. When I stepped into the room of that loyal battalion commander, his eyes were tightly closed, flying flesh and blood, broken bodies, the symphony of gunfire, I imagined, people's broken "Shanghai War" impressions, forever lingering in his soul, gnawing at his loyal heart. "Battalion Commander Li!" My friend gently called him, he opened his hazy eyes, it seemed that he was very laborious, but his eyes were still bleary.

"Oh? Who? You, Lao Mai!" He stared for a while before shouting it out. He approached us, shook hands with me humbly, smiled, and asked my name. He enthusiastically poured water and asked us to sit down. After talking for a while, we became very familiar friends. "How long have you been injured?" I asked him with concern.

"Ah, on the deep night of February 4th, I wore flowers, very ashamed, very early." He replied calmly. "Where did you wear flowers?"

"Fashionable ladies wear them by their temples, young masters wear them on the hard chests of their formal attire. We, of course, wear them on our skin. I was injured in the thigh." He coughed, and then said, "Originally, I didn't need to stay in the hospital, but I was injured by a dumdum bullet, you see, my eyes are still like a blind man!" He seemed a little emotional.

"Sacrificing for the country, injured for the nation, the flowers you wear, Battalion Commander, are unfading flowers of glory, and you should have no regrets." I comforted him, with my most sublime sympathy.

"I joined the army at the age of fourteen, and I came from the ranks. I have fought for fifteen years, and only this time did my consciousness think it had meaning. I oppose both civil wars and international wars, but eliminating the strong is the truth, the most satisfying justice - that cannot be said to be 'national feeling.' I wear flowers, and this one is truly the most fragrant, the most beautiful in color!"

"Victory is originally not a condition of war." Battalion Commander Li seemed to have a profound feeling, he continued, "This cannot be considered a purely struggle. It's just that Japanese soldiers came to hit us, and we bit the bullet and fought them. Our rifles, after firing four or five times, would get hot. What are we fighting with? Their planes scout while assisting the army in combat, and also drop non-dispersing fireworks to mark targets for the artillery." He began to shake his head, smiling bitterly and tragically. He stopped his mouth by the county river.

At that time, loneliness occupied our space, and I was afraid that he would become sentimental, so I quickly asked, "Then why were we able to resist for more than a month, and maintain the advantage?"

"Advantage?" His voice was a little dry, "Exchanged for with blood and flesh. At the beginning of the engagement, they deployed two men for every one of our brothers. Later, it was one for one, and finally, under their fierce artillery fire, it became two of them for every one of us. For a month, we used our blood to maintain the Chinese personality! Alas, the poor brothers, in the bombardment of heavy artillery and bombs, they were simply listening to their deaths."

Finally, the blood-like red clouds stained the eyes of that respectable hero, and the tears exposed the true nature of humanity. His voice was also hoarse, "We didn't have anti-aircraft guns, and we couldn't borrow them no matter where we borrowed. Later, we were fortunate to get the help of the Fifth Army, who lent us seven. Three protected the Zhenru radio station, and the regimental commanders on the front line didn't even have one to protect them. In the gentle piano sounds of the ladies, we retreated completely."

Finally, Battalion Commander Li also talked to me a lot about politics, concluding with one sentence: everyone is fighting over bones. He solemnly indicated to me that he denied his war achievements, he wanted to find his new life. I felt that Battalion Commander Li was a promising soldier in China. The credit belongs to others, the fault is mine, that kind of spirit is great!

Record of Twin Towers on the Battlefield (88) 131

— Master of Seeking Happiness Studio

Chapter Eleven: Gazing at the Governor's Pennant in a Lopsided Small Town, Grotesque Crowds of People Follow the Outriders

Otherwise. This city has no real output of local products that would benefit actual commerce. The finances were also originally impoverished. If it weren't for those passing merchants with their large consumption and purchasing power, where would you find so many good customers? But where do these merchants come from? Why do they gather here? It's still a question. This then boils down to the means by which the county magistrate becomes a lucrative and wealthy position. It turns out that these merchants are all here specifically to file lawsuits! The local customs are fierce and strong. In addition to being fully expressed in the wind-swept fishing boats and the dens of bandits gathered in the mountains, they are also extremely litigious and quick to take offense. On weekdays, they make a profit by fishing and selling salt in the sea, and by robbing homes and benefiting themselves at the expense of their neighbors. They accumulate some money and return to their hometown to buy fields and houses, still acting as law-abiding citizens. However, their heroic spirit remains, and they are privately competitive. It is difficult for them to live in peace with their neighbors. Often, for the smallest of things, such as a chicken or a wall, a disagreement will lead to a strong-willed outburst, and they are determined to gain the upper hand. But at this time, they do not use the white knives in, red knives out kind of trick to determine who is superior. They must join hands and go to the county seat and county government to file lawsuits, seeking the county magistrate to judge right and wrong, taking winning the lawsuit as the supreme glory and face. The county government in this kind of remote county also manages the judiciary, which is equivalent to running a side business with great prospects. Having good customers who file lawsuits and are willing to come to the door in an endless stream is extremely welcome. No wonder the officials have many benefits, and the resources of this street depend entirely on these people who file lawsuits to add color, and attract many lawyers and yamen runners to talk about their litigation strategies day and night, in order to obtain money through various entertaining activities such as eating, drinking, whoring, and gambling. One day, at dusk, a group of newly arrived wealthy merchants suddenly arrived at the Changxing Inn, the most famous and wealthiest inn in the county government. They were not the village elders who had come from the surrounding villages to file lawsuits, but officials from the provincial capital who had been dispatched with other public duties. The group consisted of more than ten people in total. They hired two official-style blue cloth curtained mule carts and several tall animals, guarded by four or five armed soldiers in military uniforms with box guns around their waists, walking in front of and behind the carts. They came in a mighty and imposing manner, showing off their power along the way.

Yarn and Cotton Yarn Market: Downtrend Difficult to Reverse 138

With Such Circumstances...How Can It Be Supported?

The cotton yarn market fell in the morning and rebounded in the afternoon, but the trend remained weak. With such circumstances, it is difficult to reverse. World commodity prices are falling sharply, so how can local yarn be supported? Therefore, sellers were eager to sell, and sentiment was depressed. The continuous price declines in recent days have been excessive. Today, the price broke through the 40 liang mark, and in the afternoon, it broke through the 39 liang mark. Later, those who had made profits covered their positions, and the market rebounded above the 40 liang mark. The overall situation remains dangerous, and actual demand is too sluggish.

Silk and Tea: Subtle Movements in "Chouxin Zhenmei" 145

Yesterday, in the tea market of this port, there was a slight stir in the "Chouxin Zhenmei" green tea from Wudong Tunxi and other areas. English trading houses such as Jinlong Baochang Tianxiang Dode were all actively processing it, and sales showed some activity. However, the asking price was 150 to 160 taels, slightly lower than before. Ordinary "Zhenmei" remained sluggish in the market. "Zhenmei," "Xiumei," and similar items were still being traded actively, and market prices were quite firm. Traders specializing in "Gongxi" tea from Wenzhou Yushan and other regions showed increasing interest, but negotiations with the Russian Aid Association for the upper and middle grades of goods had not yet reached a settlement. Persian merchants were also taking a wait-and-see approach, and there were no large-scale transactions reported.

New Wuyuan Tea Sales Active, Prices High 146

Spring tea stockpiled in the villages of Beiyuan, Wuyuan County, and unsold, had been suffering from the sluggishness of the Shanghai market, and there had been difficulties in finding a way to sell it. Although the price had fallen to 48 yuan a few days ago, merchants still did not dare to start processing. However, in the past two days, various firms received telegrams from Shanghai warehouses reporting a turnaround, and the selling price of "Tunwu Gongxi Zhenmei" had opened at 80 taels, 30 taels higher than in previous years. Although the "Chouxin Zhenmei" market shrank, it could still be compensated for by the other. Therefore, well-funded and daring merchants began to consider purchasing the garden tea with excellent leaf quality. It was reported that several places in Beiyuan were negotiating sales of stored tea the day before yesterday, and the market price had rebounded from 48 yuan to 58 yuan, an increase of 10 yuan compared to the price two weeks ago. The long-dormant tea market has now begun to show signs of life. If the market for "Gongzhen" and by-products in Shanghai remains firm, it will not be difficult to clear the unsold tea in the mountains within the month. Previously, merchants had paid little attention to the new "Zhangshan" tea of the highest grade because they mostly processed "Zhenmei." Now that "Gongxi" is fetching a good price, this kind of tea with excellent water content and leaves is most suitable for processing "Gongxi." Tea firms in the northern part of the county have been sending people into the mountains to find it in recent days.

Tunxi Tea Market Gradually Improving 147

The bleakness of the Tunxi tea market for the past month has been described in previous reports. Recently, firms have repeatedly received reports of improvement from the Shanghai market, with the selling price of "Gongzhen" higher than before, and news that the "Zhen" market is trending upward. Those who were previously dispirited are now regaining their appetites. Tea firms with large appetites are planning to add to their stock of tea at reduced prices. However, merchants and brokers, knowing that the Shanghai market is not bad, are confidently increasing prices and are unwilling to sell at the prices (50 yuan) that the firms are willing to pay. Therefore, there are still few who have reached agreements. As for the tea peddlers who sell to shops and stores, due to the urgent demand from North China and Tianjin, the asking price has soared to 34 yuan in recent days, which is the highest price rarely seen since tea peddlers began selling. The high-grade goods from Xiu and Wu counties have almost been completely bought up, but the demand for large quantities is not being met. Therefore, the tea market in foreign stores and trading houses in Tunxi has returned to a good state, without the depression of the previous month.

Commemoration of the Shaji Massacre 148

The Whole City Under Strict Security

Yesterday was the commemoration of the Shaji Massacre. The Chinese and foreign concessions in this city, fearing that reactionary elements would take the opportunity to riot, imposed a temporary curfew. A crowd gathering was discovered near the Eight Immortals Bridge and was dispersed by the police. Fortunately, the evening passed peacefully. The various situations are recorded below:

Strict Security: All districts under the jurisdiction of the Municipal Public Security Bureau were ordered yesterday to maintain strict security. All main roads had double posts. Police brigades, patrol car teams, and armed patrols, supervisors, and female inspectors were all dispatched to inspect pedestrians, especially in the areas of West Gate, Fangbang Bridge, North Little Gate, and East Little Gate, which were the strictest. Iron gates on the border between the Chinese and foreign concessions were only left open at Nanyang Bridge, Xie Bridge, North Little Gate, New North Gate, Old North Gate, and East Little Gate, as usual, to allow vehicles to pass through. Police stations in the Public Concession and French Concession were also ordered to step up precautions, especially in the areas of East Shanghai, West Shanghai, and the border with the Chinese Concession.

Dispersing Gatherings: Yesterday at 10:00 AM, near the Xiaocai Market in the French Concession's Eight Immortals Bridge, more than 80 people resembling workers and students were found gathering in preparation for a meeting. The political department of the French Concession police station had received a report in advance and immediately dispatched a large number of Chinese and foreign detectives to maintain strict security in the area, and immediately took measures to disperse the crowd, so no incident occurred. Peace was restored in all places in the evening, and security gradually relaxed.
